I usually go to the Starbucks across the Street if I have time before my Saturday Meetings but it was packed so I thought I'd give this spot a chance. I told the girl right off the bat that I'd be doing a review and I'd love it if I could have a new place to come instead of SB. I'm in recovery and I'm Miss Sunshine. This chick was just a ball of misery. She acted as if every word I said was like nails on a chalkboard. I felt super awkward about the entire interaction. Of course I had to wait around for my bagel. . .tick. . .tock. . .tick. .
.tock. . .oh gawd. . .anywho. I asked for ice and she only filled my cup half way. Before I left I asked the nicer chick to fill it up. Bottom line: They are too busy for their own good.  Misery was probably way overworked. They just didn't stop. It REALLY affected the customer service. Misery is a hard worker no doubt. She just needs an extra set of hands around!  Don't be cheap owners!  There are people looking for work, you're working your staff to the point of misery and I personally won't come back unless I see more help and Smiles behind that counter. If I had a better experience I wouldn't have noticed how blah the bagel was.  I really do wish your business the best.  That's all I got.< /Review>

<Review>This park is honestly a soccer park! The field has synthetic grass which is nice beacuse that means the kids won't trip on small patches of grass or holes made by the preious match. There are benches for the parents to sit and watch the games. There is a small playground area for the little ones and it has a fence around it so the kids won't run into the main road. Last but not least the bathrooms, they are clean and well maintained! The sinks actually have running water. To me that's a big deal because I have been to different parks and the bathrooms are gross! Check it out next time you are around there, this little park is a hidden little gem.</Review><GmapID>0x80dc7695ce3f0cc9:0xbb4d03cac54286d2< /GmapID></record>

< Review>
Stopped up here when one of my friends had an oil leak on his motorcycle. The water fountain works luckily, but the office itself is closed Saturday and Sunday. Considering there is no cell service on the mountain, there is a land line at the fire station across the street. One of the few places you can make a call from on the crest. Hung out here for about an hour. Beautiful views.</Review>

igloo stones</username>
< Text>
This is the information station here at the Highway 2 National Forest entrance. At this location you can purchase Daily access passes as well as annual passes. they also have lots of information about the National Forest, with trails, tours, and guides to help you navigate your way through the forest. They also have schedules and updates pertaining specific locations within the forest that close in summer and winter times. be sure to always stop by here to get the latest information about the forest. Also, it is your responsibility to protect the forest from a fire, so be safe!< /Text>

<Date>1470774919066<//Date>< Review>
If you have questions regarding sites in the Angeles Forest or just general do's and don'ts, this is the place you want to visit.

The park ranger was super funny. I had two buns on my head and she got excited and called me a bear. But besides her charm, she was super informative explaining how we couldn't go out in the forest and fire our legal firearms unless we had hunting permits. Online if you look at the information it appears to suggest you can go out to the forest and practice open firing as long as you are away from campers. But she explained how they aren't a open carry Forest. City folk don't know these things.

Overall great information.< /Review>

< Text>
Ride up through Angeles Forest all the time. Had a mechanical failure on my motorcycle while on Angeles Forest Highway. Staff let us call AAA for a tow (there is no cellular service up here) and had a set of hex wrenches that we were able to borrow.

Latrine is available on-site.<//Text>

<UserId.>110623994303657435899<//UserId.><username>Linda Lesabre<//username>< Time>
1599534726877</Time>
<rate>4</rate>< Text>
A cute little mini-park tucked along the side of the beautiful + historic Mt. Saint Mary University. Many big, shady trees + lots of pretty grass. Popular for dog walks. Many well-behaved dogs come here for off-leash play. Small garden in center. 1 working water fountain. Relatively safe area even after dark. Pretty neighborhood lends to a nice walk too. Street parking is almost always an available. Popular with students to study + stretch.  A few homeless folks do hang here now + then but I've never had any problems over the many years I've been coming here. No fenced dog area so watch them carefully.  No playground. No restrooms. No benches. Nearby mini-market 1 street away. A historical marker across street has interesting story of this place too. Worth a read. Please pick up your dog waste + trash, friends, so we can all enjoy.< /Text>

<rating>5</rating>< review>
Been coming here for years. Best pupusas out of anywhere I've been to. And ive been to alot.  They're always good. Never a bad pupusa. Even the drinks are amazing. I love their ensalada drink. It's awesome. Also try their empanada.

Yes the wait to get them can be long. But that's because they're made from scratch. And they're perfect and you can't rush perfection. So what I do Is I call ahead a good 30 minutes. And even then the wait can still be another 15 to 20 minutes. But like I said. You can't rush perfection.

Like 80%of the time the service is great. The other 20% it's not. Depends on whos working I guess. But it doesn't bother me. I'll take bad service as long as the food is amazing. Meh but that's just me.

I tell everyone i know about this place. Because I think it's that great.< /review>

<name>Fausto Varela<//name><time>1487880850539<//time><rating>5</rating><Review>As the child of a Salvadorian mother, I grew up with Salvadorian food and it's something I've grown accustomed to. That said, I'm always apprehensive about pupusas when eating out. My mom's pupusas will always be the best to me, but the pupusas here are well done.

I especially enjoy that they offer casamiento, which was delicious. The chorizo offered here was new to me, but was also very good, served on a sizzling skillet. The horchata was good and the authentic Central American stuff, which can be hard to find. It was definitely much sweeter than what I'm used to, so that is something to keep in mind.</Review>< pics>
